Definition of Miracle According to Theologians
Al-Nasafi defines the miracle with conditions and exclusions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of a prophetic miracle (mu'jiza) according to the theologians, including its three essential conditions.

Core Idea
A miracle is a custom-breaking event that proves prophethood, not sainthood or divinity.

Theologians (mutakallimun) carefully define miracles to distinguish them from other wondrous events. This lesson presents Imam al-Nasafi's definition of a miracle (mu'jiza) with its key conditions. Understanding these conditions helps prevent common confusions between prophetic miracles and saintly wonders (karamat).

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own wording come through.
Notice that the definition is precise and includes multiple conditions.
2
Identify the three conditions
The definition contains restrictions: the event must occur in dar al-taklif, it must be to prove prophethood, and it excludes claimants of divinity and saintly miracles.
Each condition serves to exclude false claims.
3
Understand the exclusion of saintly miracles
The passage explains that saints can perform custom-breaking acts (karamat), but these are not miracles because the saint does not claim prophethood. If a saint claims prophethood, they become an apostate.
This distinction is crucial in Sunni theology.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why these conditions are necessary to validate a miracle as proof of prophethood. Consider how they protect the concept of prophethood.
This connects to the broader purpose of miracles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحدها على طريقة المتكلمين أنها ظهور أمر خلاف العادة في دار التكليف لإظهار صدق مدعي النبوة مع نكول من يتحدى به عن معارضته بمثله. وإنما قيد بدار التكليف؛ لأن ما يظهره الله تعالى في الآخرة من الأمور الخارجة عن العادة، ليست بمعجزة، وإنما قلنا: لإظهار صدق مدعي النبوة ليقع الاحتراز به عما يظهر على يد مدعي الألوهية، إذ ظهور نقض المادة على يده جائز على ما نبين في خلال كلامنا - إن شاء الله تعالى - وعما يظهر على يدي الولي، لأن ظهور الناقض للعادة على يد الولي كرامة له جائز على ما نبين، إلا أنه لا يدعي النبوة، ولو ادعاها لكفر من ساعته وبطلت ولايته وصار عدوا الله، فلا تظهر على يده الكرامة بعد ذلك.
Its definition according to the method of the theologians: that it is the manifestation of a matter that breaks the custom in the abode of obligation for the purpose of manifesting the truthfulness of the claimant of prophethood, with the one who is challenged desisting from opposing it with its like. And it is restricted to the abode of obligation because what Allah the Exalted manifests in the Hereafter of matters that break the custom are not miracles. And we said 'for the purpose of manifesting the truthfulness of the claimant of prophethood' in order to exclude what appears at the hand of a claimant of divinity, for the manifestation of breaking custom at his hand is permissible as we will explain in the course of our words, God willing, and to exclude what appears at the hand of the saint, because the manifestation of the breaker of custom at the hand of the saint is a miracle (karama) for him, permissible as we will explain, except that he does not claim prophethood. If he claimed it, he would become an apostate immediately, his sainthood would be invalidated, and he would become an enemy of Allah, so no miracle (karama) would appear at his hand after that.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage defines a miracle (mu'jiza) according to the theologians (mutakallimun). It is a custom-breaking event occurring in this world of obligation (dar al-taklif) to prove the truthfulness of a prophet, with the challenger being unable to produce the like. Three conditions are highlighted: 1) It must be in dar al-taklif, excluding afterlife wonders. 2) It must be to prove prophethood, excluding acts of those claiming divinity (since those cannot be true). 3) It excludes saintly wonders (karamat), which do not accompany a prophecy claim. If a saint claims prophethood, he becomes an apostate and his karama ceases.

Key Terms
خلاف العادة
دار التكليف
معجزة
نبوة
ولي
كرامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People sometimes think any supernatural event performed by a pious person is a miracle (mu'jiza).
Correction: Only prophets perform miracles; saints perform karamat. The key difference is the claim of prophethood.

Checkpoint
Why does the theologian definition restrict miracles to the 'abode of obligation' (dar al-taklif)?
A) Because afterlife wonders are not miracles
B) Because saints can only have miracles in this life
C) Because only prophets exist in this world
D) Because miracles must be possible

Key Takeaway
A prophetic miracle is a custom-breaking event in this world that proves a man's claim to prophethood, and it must be distinguished from saintly wonders.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear claims of miraculous events today, do you instinctively accept them as signs from Allah? How does this lesson's definition challenge you to be more discerning about what truly constitutes a prophetic miracle?
?
This lesson distinguishes between prophetic miracles and saintly honors. How does this affect your understanding of the role of prophets vs. saints in your own faith? Are you guilty of attributing prophetic authority to saints or spiritual leaders?
?
The miracle's purpose is to prove truthfulness of a prophecy claim. Has there been a time when you accepted a miracle story without considering its source or purpose? How will you apply the conditions from this lesson to evaluate such claims in the future?

How the Miracle Indicates the Prophet's Truthfulness
Begins explaining the reasoning linking a miracle to the prophet's veracity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first part of the kalam argument showing how a miracle proves a prophet's truthfulness.

Core Idea
A miracle confirms the prophet because God would not support a liar.

This lesson begins the logical explanation of how a miracle indicates the truthfulness of a prophet. The argument starts with two foundational premises: that God hears the prophet's claim and that the miracle is beyond human ability. Understanding these premises is essential before the conclusion is drawn.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic fragment
Carefully read the incomplete Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the key terms: دلالة, صدق, سامع, مقدور البشر.
The text is cut off but the main premises are clear.
2
Identify the two premises
The author states two facts: (1) God hears the claimant, (2) the miracle is beyond human capacity. These are the basis for the conclusion that the miracle confirms truthfulness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما وجه كيفية دلالتها على صدق الآتي بها، فإنا نعلم أن الله تعالى سامع لما يقوله هذا المدعي، وأن ما يظهر على يده خارج عن مقدور البشر بل عن [؟]
As for the aspect of how it indicates the truthfulness of the one who brings it, we know that Allah Most High hears what this claimant says, and that what appears at his hand is beyond the capacity of humans, rather beyond [؟]
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage begins to explain the logical connection between a miracle and the truthfulness of the prophet who performs it. The argument presented is that we know with certainty that God hears the claim of the prophet (that he is a messenger). We also know that the miracle that appears at the prophet's hand is outside the capacity of humans (and possibly other creatures), meaning it can only come from God. Therefore, since God is truthful and would not support a liar with a supernatural act, the act must be a confirmation of the prophet's truthfulness. The text is incomplete due to the page break, but the core reasoning is established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The text only provides the two premises; the conclusion (that the miracle confirms truthfulness) is inferred and will be completed in the subsequent lesson.

Checkpoint

D) Because the miracle defies logic

Key Takeaway
The miracle's indication of truth rests on two certainties: God's hearing of the claim and the miracle's supernatural origin.

Miracles as Divine Confirmation of Prophethood
Nasafi proves miracles as divine confirmation via analogies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of how a miracle serves as divine confirmation of a prophet's claim, using analogies from everyday situations.

Core Idea
A miracle is Allah's unambiguous 'Yes' to a prophet's claim.

Nasafi begins by establishing that breaking the natural norm is an act only Allah can perform. He then provides vivid analogies to show how such an act, when performed after a claim of prophethood, functions as direct divine confirmation—like a king moving a tree to verify his messenger. This lesson walks through those analogies to clarify the logical proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core claim
Read the first sentence carefully: the breaking of the norm is only within Allah's power. This is the foundation.
2
Examine the first two analogies
Nasafi gives a 'secrets' analogy and a 'ring' analogy. See how each shows that a unique action confirms a claim.
Notice he says speech can be mocked, but action cannot.
3
Understand the king's tree analogy
This detailed analogy is the centerpiece. A king's exclusive power to move a tree verifies a messenger. Work through the steps.
This analogy mirrors the divine miracle.
4
Connect to divine confirmation
The appearance of the miracle after the claim produces certain knowledge that Allah is confirming the prophet.
Nasafi says it is like hearing the king say 'You have spoken the truth'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدور جميع الخلق ولا قدرة عليه إلا الله تعالى، فإذا ادعى الرسالة، ثم قال آية صدق دعواي أن الله أرسلني أن يفعل الله كذا ففعل الله تعالى ذلك كان تصديقا من الله تعالى له فيما يدعي من الرسالة بما فعل من نقض المادة، فيكون ذلك كقوله عقيب دعواه هذه صدقت نظيره. وأن من أرسله غيره من البشر إلى آخر فقال الرسول للمرسل، اكتب لي شيئًا من الأسرار التي كانت بينك وبينه فكتب له، وعلم المرسل إليه أن لا إطلاع على تلك الأسرار لغير المرسل كان ذلك دلالة صادقة على صدق مدعي الرسالة. وكذا لو قال رجل لصاحب الوديعة بين يدي المودع، إن كنت صادقا فيما أدعى من أمرك إياي بأخذ وديعتك منك فناولني خاتمك فناوله كان ذلك دليلاً على صدقه، كما لو قال صدقت بل أبلغ إذ القول به يحتمل الاستهزاء وهذا مما لا احتمال فيه بوجه من الوجوه، وكذا نظيره أن ملكا من الملوك لو كان في قصره شجرة عظيمة تقرر عند أهل مملكته وسكان حضرته أن لا قدرة لأحد من أهل قصر الملك على تحريك تلك الشجرة إلا الملك، ثم أن رجلاً من أهل القصر خرج إلى أهل البلدة وأخبرهم أنه رسول الملك إليهم وأن الملك يأمرهم بكذا وينهاهم عن كذا فكذبه أهل البلد في إدعاءه الرسالة من الملك إليهم، فنادى هذا الرجل بصوت يعلم أن الملك يسمعه لا محالة، أيها الملك أنك أرسلتني إلى رعيتك من أهل بلدتك وأمرتني أن أبلغ إليهم رسالة كذا بلغت إليهم فكذبوني في الرسالة، فإن كنت أرسلتني إليهم وكنت صادقًا فيما ادعيت من رسالتك إليهم فحرك الشجرة التي في قصرك ليكون تحركها آية صدقي فتحركت الشجرة بمرأى من أهل البلدة عقيب هذا النداء، كان ذلك دليلاً على صدق مقالة الرسول، وكان بمنزلة ما لو سمعوا من الملك أن قال للرسول: صدقت فيما ادعيت من رسالتي، أو قال لأهل البلدة: إنه صادق فيما بلغ إليكم من رسالتي، فكذا هذا. ثم ظهور الناقض للعادة عقيب دعوى الملك للرسالة، يوجب العلم يقينا أن الله تعالى هو الذي فعل ذلك إذ لا قدرة لغيره على مثل ذلك الفعل، ثم ذلك منه تصديق له فيدل ذلك على صدقه لا محالة، ثم ظهور مثله على يدي الكاذب في دعوى الرسالة ممتنع. واختلف المتكلمون في وجه امتناعه فقال من قال من أصحابنا باستدراك الحكمة والسفه والقبيح والحسن بمجرد العقول أن جهة امتناعه أنه لو ظهر ذلك على يد المتنبي، ولا دليل على صدق النبي إلا هذا لكان فيه التسوية بين الصادق والكاذب والحق والباطل، وسد طريق الوصول إلى الحق أصلاً وذا خارج من الحكمة، حتى إن ظهور ناقض العادة على يدي المتأله لما لم يكن سادًا طريق الوصول إلى الحق، ولا موجبًا التسوية بين الحق والباطل والمحق والمبطل لما في شخصه من أمارات الحدوث، ودلائل كونه كاذبًا في دعواه كان ذلك ممكنا ممتنع بخلاف المتنبئ فإنه ليس في ذاته ما يدل على كذبه إذ هو من جوهر صادق في الدعوى لا فرق بينهما من حيث الذات فلا فرقان بينهما إلا من جهة المعجزة الناقضة للعادة فكان في ظهورها على يدي الكاذب ما مر من التسوية بين الحق والباطل وسد طريق الوصول إلى الحق
Not within the power of all creation and no one has power over it except Allah the Exalted. So when he claims prophethood, then says as a sign of the truth of my claim that Allah sent me, let Allah do such-and-such, and Allah the Exalted does that, then that is a confirmation from Allah the Exalted to him regarding what he claims of prophethood by what He did of breaking the norm. Thus it is like His saying after this claim: 'You have spoken the truth,' its analogy. And if another human sent him to another, and the messenger said to the one who sent him: 'Write for me some of the secrets that were between you and him,' so he wrote for him, and the one sent to knew that there is no access to those secrets for other than the sender, that would be a true indication of the truthfulness of the claimant of prophethood. Likewise, if a man said to the depositary in the presence of the depositor: 'If you are truthful in what I claim regarding your order to me to take your deposit from you, then hand me your ring,' and he handed it to him, that would be evidence of his truthfulness, just as if he said 'You have spoken the truth' or even more, because speech admits of mockery, but this has no possibility of mockery in any way. And likewise its analogy: If a king had in his palace a great tree, established among the people of his kingdom and residents of his city that no one from the people of the king's palace has power to move that tree except the king, then a man from the people of the palace went out to the people of the town and informed them that he is the messenger of the king to them, and that the king commands them thus and forbids them thus, and the people of the town denied his claim of prophethood from the king to them; then this man called out with a voice that he knew the king would hear without doubt: 'O king, you sent me to your subjects from your townspeople and ordered me to convey to them such-and-such a message; I conveyed it to them, but they denied me regarding the message. If you sent me to them and I am truthful in what I claimed of your message to them, then move the tree that is in your palace so that its movement becomes a sign of my truthfulness,' and the tree moved in sight of the townspeople after this call, that would be evidence of the truth of the messenger's statement, and it would be in the position of if they heard from the king that he said to the messenger: 'You have spoken the truth in what you claimed of my message,' or he said to the townspeople: 'He is truthful in what he conveyed to you of my message.' So likewise this. Then the appearance of the breaker of norm after the claim of the king to prophethood necessarily produces certain knowledge that Allah the Exalted is the one who did that, since no one else has power over such an act; then that is from Him confirmation of him, so it indicates his truthfulness without doubt. Then the appearance of the like of it on the hand of a liar in the claim of prophethood is impossible. The mutakallimun differed concerning the aspect of its impossibility: Those of our companions who hold that wisdom, foolishness, evil, and good are discerned by pure reason said that the aspect of its impossibility is that if that were to appear on the hand of a false prophet, and there is no proof of the truthfulness of the prophet except this, then it would entail equalization between the truthful and the liar, truth and falsehood, and blocking the way to arriving at truth entirely, and that is outside wisdom. So much so that the appearance of a breaker of norm on the hand of a devotee (mutā'allih) – since it does not block the way to arriving at truth, nor necessitate equalization between truth and falsehood and the truthful and the false, due to what is in his person of signs of origination and proofs that he is false in his claim – that would be possible but impossible? unlike the false prophet, for in his essence there is nothing that indicates his falsehood, since he is of the same substance as one truthful in the claim; there is no distinction between them in terms of essence, so there is no distinction between them except from the aspect of the miracle that breaks the norm. Thus in its appearance on the hand of the liar there would be what was mentioned of equalization between truth and falsehood and blocking the way to arriving at truth.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a proof and explanation of how miracles function as divine confirmation of prophethood, and why it is impossible for a false prophet to perform a miracle. The author, Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi, begins by stating that breaking the norm (naqd al-‘ādah) is an act that only Allah can perform. When a claimant to prophethood says, 'If Allah has sent me, let Him do such-and-such,' and Allah does it, that act serves as divine confirmation (taṣdīq) of his claim, equivalent to Allah saying 'You have spoken the truth' after the claim. Nasafi then provides analogies: a messenger who produces a secret known only to the sender and the recipient; a depositor who hands over his ring as proof of his instruction; and a detailed analogy of a king with a unique tree that only he can move. In each case, the extraordinary act performed after the claim proves the claimant's truthfulness because it is an unambiguous sign. The passage then moves to the second point: it is impossible for a miracle (nāqiḍ al-‘ādah) to appear on the hand of a false prophet (mutanabbī). The mutakallimūn differed on the reason. Nasafi reports the view of his school (ashābunā) who hold that good and evil are known by reason alone. Their argument is: if a false prophet could perform a miracle, and the only proof of true prophethood is the miracle, then there would be no way to distinguish truth from falsehood; this would equalize truth and falsehood and block the path to truth, which is contrary to divine wisdom (ḥikmah). In contrast, a miracle on a devotee (mutā'allih) does not block the path because the devotee's person contains signs of being created (amārāt al-ḥudūth) and proofs of falsehood in his claim (since he does not claim prophethood). But a false prophet is essentially similar to a true prophet; there is no intrinsic difference except through the miracle. Therefore, allowing a miracle on a false prophet would lead to the unacceptable equalization of truth and falsehood.

Key Terms
ناقض العادة
المعجزة
التصديق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the king's tree analogy, what does the movement of the tree represent?
A) The power of the messenger
B) The king's confirmation of the messenger's truth
C) The people's acceptance of the message
D) The tree's natural movement

Key Takeaway
A miracle is an unambiguous divine act that confirms a prophet's truthfulness, just as a king moving his unique tree confirms a messenger.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After reading Nasafi's analogy of the king's tree, reflect: when you hear about the miracles of Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ), such as the splitting of the moon, do you respond with the same certainty as the townspeople who saw the tree move? If not, what is holding you back? Pray to Allah to remove your doubts and resolve to study the prophetic proofs with a sincere heart.
?
Nasafi argues that an action (like the tree moving) is a stronger proof than words because words can be mockery. Think of a time when you doubted a claim because of empty words. How does this lesson challenge you to seek action-based evidence in matters of faith? Commit to examining the proofs of prophethood with the same standard.
?
If you were the messenger in the analogy standing before the king's palace, would you have the courage to call out to the king, risking embarrassment if the tree did not move? The prophets had complete trust in Allah's support. How strong is your trust that Allah will confirm what is true? Ask yourself: am I willing to stake my reputation on the truth of Islam as the prophets did?

Why False Prophets Cannot Perform Miracles
Nasafi argues why false prophets cannot perform miracles, using rational grounds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational argument that a false prophet cannot perform a miracle, because it would nullify the distinction between truth and falsehood.

Core Idea
If a liar could work miracles, truth and falsehood would be indistinguishable.

After establishing that miracles confirm true prophets, Nasafi tackles the crucial question: Could a false prophet also perform a miracle? He explains that this is impossible, and reports the reasoning of the school that good and evil are known by reason. The key insight is that allowing miracles on liars would make it impossible to know the truth, contradicting divine wisdom.

Guided Path
1
Read the impossibility claim
Nasafi states clearly: the appearance of a miracle on a false prophet is impossible. This is the conclusion he will justify.
2
Identify the school's reasoning
The school that holds good and evil are known by reason argues: if a false prophet could do a miracle, and the miracle is the only proof, then truth and falsehood would be equalized.
This is a rational argument, not textual.
3
Contrast with a devotee (mutā'allih)
Nasafi notes that a miracle on a pious non-prophet is possible because his person shows signs of being created and not claiming prophethood, so it doesn't confuse the path.
The phrase 'impossible? unlike the false prophet' is tricky; understand it as 'possible, unlike the false prophet.'
4
Understand the essence argument
A false prophet and a true prophet are indistinguishable in essence; only the miracle differentiates them. If the liar could produce a miracle, there would be no way to tell them apart.
This is the heart of the impossibility.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

نقض المادة، فيكون ذلك كقوله عقيب دعواه هذه صدقت نظيره. وأن من أرسله غيره من البشر إلى آخر فقال الرسول للمرسل، اكتب لي شيئًا من الأسرار التي كانت بينك وبينه فكتب له، وعلم المرسل إليه أن لا إطلاع على الملك أن قال للرسول: صدقت فيما ادعيت من رسالتي، أو قال لأهل البلدة: إنه صادق فيما بلغ إليكم من رسالتي، فكذا هذا. ثم ظهور الناقض للعادة عقيب دعوى الملك للرسالة، يوجب العلم يقينا أن الله تعالى هو الذي فعل ذلك إذ لا قدرة لغيره على مثل ذلك الفعل، ثم ذلك منه تصديق له فيدل ذلك على صدقه لا محالة، ثم ظهور مثله على يدي الكاذب في دعوى الرسالة ممتنع. واختلف المتكلمون في وجه امتناعه فقال من قال من أصحابنا باستدراك الحكمة والسفه والقبيح والحسن بمجرد العقول أن جهة امتناعه أنه لو ظهر ذلك على يد المتنبي، ولا دليل على صدق النبي إلا هذا لكان فيه التسوية بين الصادق والكاذب والحق والباطل، وسد طريق الوصول إلى الحق أصلاً وذا خارج من الحكمة، حتى إن ظهور ناقض العادة على يدي المتأله لما لم يكن سادًا طريق الوصول إلى الحق، ولا موجبًا التسوية بين الحق والباطل والمحق والمبطل لما في شخصه من أمارات الحدوث، ودلائل كونه كاذبًا في دعواه كان ذلك ممكنا ممتنع بخلاف المتنبئ فإنه ليس في ذاته ما يدل على كذبه إذ هو من جوهر صادق في الدعوى لا فرق بينهما من حيث الذات فلا فرقان بينهما إلا من جهة المعجزة الناقضة للعادة فكان في ظهورها على يدي الكاذب ما مر من التسوية بين الحق والباطل وسد طريق الوصول إلى الحق
Not within the power of all creation and no one has power over it except Allah the Exalted. So when he claims prophethood, then says as a sign of the truth of my claim that Allah sent me, let Allah do such-and-such, and Allah the Exalted does that, then that is a confirmation from Allah the Exalted to him regarding what he claims of prophethood by what He did of breaking the norm. Thus it is like His saying after this claim: 'You have spoken the truth,' its analogy. And if another human sent him to another, and the messenger said to the one who sent him: 'Write for me some of the secrets that were between you and him,' so he wrote for him, and the one sent to knew that there is no access to those secrets for other than the sender, that would be a true indication of the truthfulness of the claimant of prophethood. Likewise, if a man said to the depositary in the presence of the depositor: 'If you are truthful in what I claim regarding your order to me to take your deposit from you, then hand me your ring,' and he handed it to him, that would be evidence of his truthfulness, just as if he said 'You have spoken the truth' or even more, because speech admits of mockery, but this has no possibility of mockery in any way. And likewise its analogy: If a king had in his palace a great tree, established among the people of his kingdom and residents of his city that no one from the people of the king's palace has power to move that tree except the king, then a man from the people of the palace went out to the people of the town and informed them that he is the messenger of the king to them, and that the king commands them thus and forbids them thus, and the people of the town denied his claim of prophethood from the king to them; then this man called out with a voice that he knew the king would hear without doubt: 'O king, you sent me to your subjects from your townspeople and ordered me to convey to them such-and-such a message; I conveyed it to them, but they denied me regarding the message. If you sent me to them and I am truthful in what I claimed of your message to them, then move the tree that is in your palace so that its movement becomes a sign of my truthfulness,' and the tree moved in sight of the townspeople after this call, that would be evidence of the truth of the messenger's statement, and it would be in the position of if they heard from the king that he said to the messenger: 'You have spoken the truth in what you claimed of my message,' or he said to the townspeople: 'He is truthful in what he conveyed to you of my message.' So likewise this. Then the appearance of the breaker of norm after the claim of the king to prophethood necessarily produces certain knowledge that Allah the Exalted is the one who did that, since no one else has power over such an act; then that is from Him confirmation of him, so it indicates his truthfulness without doubt. Then the appearance of the like of it on the hand of a liar in the claim of prophethood is impossible. The mutakallimun differed concerning the aspect of its impossibility: Those of our companions who hold that wisdom, foolishness, evil, and good are discerned by pure reason said that the aspect of its impossibility is that if that were to appear on the hand of a false prophet, and there is no proof of the truthfulness of the prophet except this, then it would entail equalization between the truthful and the liar, truth and falsehood, and blocking the way to arriving at truth entirely, and that is outside wisdom. So much so that the appearance of a breaker of norm on the hand of a devotee (mutā'allih) – since it does not block the way to arriving at truth, nor necessitate equalization between truth and falsehood and the truthful and the false, due to what is in his person of signs of origination and proofs that he is false in his claim – that would be possible but impossible? unlike the false prophet, for in his essence there is nothing that indicates his falsehood, since he is of the same substance as one truthful in the claim; there is no distinction between them in terms of essence, so there is no distinction between them except from the aspect of the miracle that breaks the norm. Thus in its appearance on the hand of the liar there would be what was mentioned of equalization between truth and falsehood and blocking the way to arriving at truth.
Source pages p. 38

Commentary
This passage is a proof and explanation of how miracles function as divine confirmation of prophethood, and why it is impossible for a false prophet to perform a miracle. The author, Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi, begins by stating that breaking the norm (naqd al-‘ādah) is an act that only Allah can perform. When a claimant to prophethood says, 'If Allah has sent me, let Him do such-and-such,' and Allah does it, that act serves as divine confirmation (taṣdīq) of his claim, equivalent to Allah saying 'You have spoken the truth' after the claim. Nasafi then provides analogies: a messenger who produces a secret known only to the sender and the recipient; a depositor who hands over his ring as proof of his instruction; and a detailed analogy of a king with a unique tree that only he can move. In each case, the extraordinary act performed after the claim proves the claimant's truthfulness because it is an unambiguous sign. The passage then moves to the second point: it is impossible for a miracle (nāqiḍ al-‘ādah) to appear on the hand of a false prophet (mutanabbī). The mutakallimūn differed on the reason. Nasafi reports the view of his school (ashābunā) who hold that good and evil are known by reason alone. Their argument is: if a false prophet could perform a miracle, and the only proof of true prophethood is the miracle, then there would be no way to distinguish truth from falsehood; this would equalize truth and falsehood and block the path to truth, which is contrary to divine wisdom (ḥikmah). In contrast, a miracle on a devotee (mutā'allih) does not block the path because the devotee's person contains signs of being created (amārāt al-ḥudūth) and proofs of falsehood in his claim (since he does not claim prophethood). But a false prophet is essentially similar to a true prophet; there is no intrinsic difference except through the miracle. Therefore, allowing a miracle on a false prophet would lead to the unacceptable equalization of truth and falsehood.

Key Terms
المتنبي
التسوية بين الحق والباطل
الحكمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that any supernatural event performed by a false prophet could still be considered a miracle, or that Allah may test people by allowing false prophets to perform miracles.
Correction: Nasafi argues that this would lead to complete confusion between truth and falsehood, which divine wisdom prevents. A false prophet cannot perform a true miracle because that would undermine the very purpose of prophethood.

Checkpoint
According to the rational argument presented by Nasafi's school, why is a miracle impossible on a false prophet?
A) Because a false prophet lacks belief in Allah
B) Because it would equalize truth and falsehood and block the path to truth
C) Because miracles require a pure lineage
D) Because false prophets are punished by Allah immediately

Key Takeaway
A false prophet cannot perform a miracle because that would make truth and falsehood indistinguishable, contradicting divine wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the only proof of a prophet is a miracle that breaks the norm, and you have no direct experience of such miracles today, how do you personally verify the truth of Muhammad’s prophethood? Are you relying on something other than your own investigation? What would happen if you did not take that step?
?
The passage says a false prophet has no intrinsic mark of falsehood. Think about your own life: where do you need to be more discerning about truth claims in religion? Are there any teachings or leaders you follow without clear evidence, simply because they seem similar to the truth? What sign would convince you if you were being deceived?
?
The devotee performs wonders but does not seek recognition. Consider someone in your life who serves Allah quietly without seeking fame. How does their humility challenge your own desire for recognition? Could your pursuit of status ever put you in the position of a false claimant—seeking authority without divine commission?

The Proof from Specialized Knowledge for the Necessity of Prophethood
Nasafi argues for prophethood's necessity via specialized knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that the existence of specialized knowledge (like medicine and astronomy) that cannot be attained by senses or reason alone proves that prophethood must have existed in past times.

Core Idea
Specialized knowledge points to a divine teacher — prophets.

Imam Nasafi presents a compelling argument for the establishment of prophethood in past times. He observes that certain bodies of knowledge—such as medicine and astronomy—cannot be fully acquired through human senses or intellect alone. The fact that such knowledge exists and is transmitted through chains of teachers ultimately traces back to a divine source, confirming that prophets were sent by Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation to get a sense of the argument's flow.
The passage ends incompletely at the page break, but the main argument is clear.
2
Identify the two topics
Notice that Nasafi begins by stating two matters: general establishment of prophethood and specific identification of prophets. This lesson focuses on the first.
3
Follow the proof from substances
The proof starts with substances (jawahir) being foods, poisons, and medicines. See how he argues that distinguishing them is impossible by senses or experiment alone.
Key concept: tawqifi (divinely taught).
4
Examine the illustrative examples
Nasafi provides examples from medicine (Hippocrates and Asclepius) and astronomy to show that even deniers trace knowledge to a divine source.
The astronomy example is cut off but reinforces the same point.
5
Reflect on the logical necessity
Consider why the chain of teaching must end with a creator who directly informed a prophet. This is the core of the argument.
Ask yourself: Could there be any other ultimate source?

وإذا علم هذا فبعد ذلك يحتاج إلى التكلم في موضعين: أحدهما في أن الرسالة قد ثبت في الجملة لا محالة فيما مضى من الأزمنة. والثاني : في إثبات رسالة بعض الرسل على طريق التعيين. ونتكلم في الفصلين جميعًا بما يوجب صحة ما ندعي في كل فصل – إن شاء الله تعالى. ثم الدليل على أن الرسالة تثبت فيما مضى من الأزمنة ما مر من أن الجواهر الموجودة في العالم منقسمة إلى أغذية وسموم وأدوية، ولا وصول إلى الامتياز بين البعض منها والبعض بالتجربة، ولا بقاء للأبدان بدون تناول الأغذية ورأينا الناس من اهتدوا إليها وإلى معرفة طبائعها ومعرفة مقادير الأدوية التي تتعلق بها المصلحة ولا تحصل بالنقصان منها المصلحة وتحصل بالزيادة عليها المضرة مع أن لا وقوف بشيء من الحواس على شيء منها ولا بالعقول، إذ أصح خليقة الله تعالى حسّاً وأوفرهم عقلاً يمكنه الوصول إلى ذلك ما لم يختلف إلى أستاذ حاذق حصل له العلم بذلك من غيره، فثبت أن من علم ذلك علم بأخباره غيره إياه لا بحسه وعقله لقصور علم غيره عنه مع مساواته في العقل والحس إلى أن ينتهي العلم بذلك إلى إخبار من له العلم بحقيقة كل من ذلك لما أنه خلقه على ما خلقه، وفي ذلك أبين دليل على ثبوت الرسالة فيما مضى لبعض من اصطفاه الله تعالى لذلك وأكرمه بإعلامه إياه طبائع هذه الجواهر ولهذا اضطر أهل العلم بطبائع هذه الجواهر المنكرين للرسالة إلى الاعتراف بأن العلم بطبائعها توقيفي فإنهم مهما قيل لهم ممن أخذتم العلم بطبائع هذه الأشياء؟ قالوا من بقراط؟ فإذا قيل لهم : وممن أخذه بقراط؟ قالوا: من أسغلينوس الإمام الذي عرج بروحه إلى السماء فاطلع عليها ، وكذا العلم بالنجوم وهيئة الأفلاك وطبائع الكواكب وكيفية سيرها والسعد فيها والنحس ، وأحكام الاتصالات بينها لن يتوصل إلى ذلك إلا بالتوقيف لتعذر الحواس والعقول عن ذلك، ولهذا لم يقف على ذلك أحد من أرباب الحواس السليمة والعقول الوافرة، ولهذا اضطر أهل النجوم
And when this is known, then after that we need to speak on two matters: one of them is that prophethood is established in general necessarily in past times; and the second is the establishment of the prophethood of some messengers by way of specification. And we will speak in both chapters with what necessitates the correctness of what we claim in each chapter, if Allah wills. Then the proof that prophethood is established in past times is what has passed: that the substances existing in the world are divided into foods, poisons, and medicines, and there is no way to distinguish between some of them and others by experiment, and no survival of bodies without consuming foods. And we see people who are guided to them and to knowledge of their natures and knowledge of the quantities of medicines by which benefit is achieved — benefit is not obtained by decrease from them, and harm is obtained by increase upon them — while there is no perception of anything of them by any of the senses nor by the intellects. For the soundest of creation of Allah in sense and the most abundant of them in intellect cannot attain to that unless he attends upon a skilled teacher from whom he has acquired that knowledge. So it is established that whoever knows that, knows it by the information of another given to him, not by his sense and intellect, due to the deficiency of the knowledge of others compared to him despite equality in intellect and sense, until that knowledge ends at the information of one who has knowledge of the reality of each of that, because he created it as he created it. And in that is the clearest proof of the establishment of prophethood in past times for some of those whom Allah chose for that and honored by informing him of the natures of these substances. And for this reason, the people knowledgeable in the natures of these substances — the deniers of prophethood — are forced to admit that the knowledge of their natures is tawqifi (divinely taught). For whenever it is said to them: 'From whom did you take the knowledge of the natures of these things?' They say: 'From Hippocrates.' And when it is said to them: 'And from whom did Hippocrates take it?' They say: 'From Asclepius, the imam whose spirit ascended to heaven and was informed of them.' Similarly, knowledge of the stars, the configuration of the orbs, the natures of the planets, the manner of their movement, the auspicious and inauspicious among them, and the rulings of conjunctions between them — one cannot attain to that except by tawqif, because the senses and intellects are incapable of that. And for this reason, none of the possessors of sound senses and abundant intellects have stood upon that. And for this reason, the people of the stars are forced...
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage presents a proof for the establishment of prophethood in past times. It begins by stating the two topics that remain after the previous discussion: first, that prophethood is established in general in past ages; second, establishing the prophethood of specific messengers. The author then provides the proof for the first topic. The proof is based on the observation that the substances in the world (jawahir) are of three types: foods, poisons, and medicines. Humans cannot distinguish between these through mere experiment (tajriba) or sensory perception, yet survival depends on consuming food. Even the most perfect human in senses and intellect cannot learn the properties and correct dosages of medicines without studying under a skilled teacher. This knowledge is acquired by instruction, not by sense or reason. The chain of instruction must ultimately go back to someone who knows the true natures of these substances because he created them — this is a divine teacher, i.e., a prophet. Therefore, the existence of such specialized, non-empirical knowledge in human history proves that prophethood existed in the past. The author supports this by noting that even those who deny prophethood (like the ancient physicians) are forced to admit that their knowledge is tawqifi (divinely taught). For example, they trace their medical knowledge to Hippocrates, and Hippocrates' knowledge to Asclepius, who is said to have ascended to heaven and been informed of these matters. Similarly, astronomy — knowledge of celestial bodies, orbits, and astrological judgments — cannot be attained through senses or reason alone, and its practitioners also trace their knowledge to divine teaching. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the argument is clear: the existence of such knowledge that is unattainable by ordinary means necessitates a source of divine revelation, which is prophethood.

Key Terms
الرسالة
الجواهر
توقيفي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that empirical knowledge alone suffices to learn properties of substances, but the argument shows that even the greatest minds cannot discover these without teaching, implying divine origin.
Correction: The proof demonstrates that specialized knowledge like medicine and astronomy cannot be attained by senses or reason alone; it must be taught, and the ultimate teacher is Allah through a prophet.

Checkpoint
According to the proof, what is the ultimate source of knowledge about the natures of food, poisons, and medicines?

B) Experimentation over many generations.
C) Divine teaching through a prophet.
D) Astrological observations.

Key Takeaway
The existence of specialized knowledge that cannot be acquired by human senses or reason alone proves that prophethood must have existed in past times.

?
If even the most intelligent humans need a teacher to grasp the properties of substances, what does that imply about your need for divine guidance in matters of faith? Are you actively seeking that guidance, or relying on your own intellect?

Prophethood

Proof of Prophethood from the Need for Divine Teaching
Nasafi argues for past prophethood via the necessity of divine teaching for specialised knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Nasafi uses the necessity of a teacher for specialised knowledge to argue that prophethood must have been established in the past through divine revelation.

Core Idea
Specialised knowledge requires a chain of teachers ending with the Creator.

Nasafi presents a cumulative argument that certain types of knowledge—like medicine, astronomy, and language—cannot be attained by human senses or intellect alone. This forces us to conclude that there must have been a divine teacher, i.e., a prophet, who received this knowledge directly from God. In this lesson, we'll examine the main proof and its historical examples.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: first a general argument, then specific examples from medicine, astronomy, crafts, and language.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Understand the core argument
Identify the key point: substances are divided into foods, poisons, medicines; humans cannot distinguish them by experiment or senses; we learn from teachers, ending with the Creator.
The argument relies on the impossibility of infinite regress.
3
Examine the historical proofs
Look at how Nasafi uses the examples of Hippocrates/Asclepius and Hermes/Idris to show that even those who deny revelation admit a divine origin.
This reinforces the necessity of prophethood.
4
Consider the extended examples
Reflect on the other domains: crafts, animal training, trade, geography, and especially language. Why does Nasafi include language?
Language shows that even conventions need an original revealed language.
5
Conclude the lesson
Summarise how all these points together prove that prophethood must have occurred in the past.

الدليل على ثبوت الرسالة في الأزمنة الماضية ما مر من أن الجواهر الموجودة في العالم منقسمة إلى أغذية وسموم وأدوية، ولا وصول إلى الامتياز بين البعض منها والبعض بالتجربة، ولا بقاء للأبدان بدون تناول الأغذية ورأينا الناس من اهتدوا إليها وإلى معرفة طبائعها ومعرفة مقادير الأدوية التي تتعلق بها المصلحة ولا تحصل بالنقصان منها المصلحة وتحصل بالزيادة عليها المضرة مع أن لا وقوف بشيء من الحواس على شيء منها ولا بالعقول، إذ أصح خليقة الله تعالى حساً وأوفرهم عقلاً يمكنه الوصول إلى ذلك ما لم يختلف إلى أستاذ حاذق حصل له العلم بذلك من غيره، فثبت أن من علم ذلك علم بأخباره غيره إياه لا بحسه وعقله لقصور علم وأكرمه بإعلامه إياه طبائع هذه الجواهر ولهذا اضطر أهل العلم بطبائع هذه الجواهر المنكرين للرسالة إلى الاعتراف بأن العلم بطبائعها توقيفي فإنهم مهما قيل لهم ممن أخذتم العلم بطبائع هذه الأشياء؟ قالوا من بقراط؟ فإذا قيل لهم : وممن أخذه بقراط؟ قالوا: من أسغلينوس الإمام الذي عرج بروحه إلى السماء فاطلع عليها ، وكذا العلم بالنجوم وهيئة الأفلاك وطبائع الكواكب وكيفية سيرها والسعد فيها والنحس ، وأحكام الاتصالات بينها لن يتوصل إلى ذلك إلا بالتوقيف لتعذر الحواس والعقول عن ذلك، ولهذا لم يقف على ذلك أحد من أرباب الحواس السليمة والعقول الوافرة، ولهذا اضطر أهل النجوم حين سئلوا عن ذلك إلى أن قالوا: بدء معرفته من قيل هرمس الحكيم وقد عرج بروحه إلى السماء، فكانت في ملكوت السماوات وعرف ذلك كله مشاهدة. وزعم بعض من ادعى العلم بالحقائق أن هرمس هو اسم إدريس عليه السلام، عند أهل المغرب في علم يعرفونه بهذا الاسم، وأهل التواريخ يزعمون أن علم النجوم نزل على إدريس عليه السلام. وهذا من أبين الدلائل أن ذلك كله ثبت بطريق الوحي من الله تعالى. وكذا العلم بالحرف التي بها قوام المعاش واتخاذ الستر والكن والوقاية من الحر والبرد. وكذا العلم بكيفية رياضة الدواب الصعبة مما ليس يعلم بالتأمل أنها لأي منفعة خلقت وبأي وجه يمكن رياضتها وتذليل صعابها وإيناس نافرها ومستوحشها. وكذا العلم بأنواع التجارات التي لا يقوم للناس دين ولا دنيا إلا بها. وكذا العلم بما يفرق بين حوائجهم فى البلدان لن يثبت إلا بالتوقيف لقصور العقول والحواس عن الوقوف على ذلك. وكذا العلم بطرق البلدان، وكذا العلم بالألسن إذ لا وجه إلى الاصطلاح إلا بعد ثبوت العلم بلسان ليتوصل بمعرفة ذلك اللسان إلى الاصطلاح على لسان آخر إذ لا وصول إلى ذلك إلا بعد وقوف المصطلحين بعضهم على ما في ضمير البعض، فإذا لابد من كون لسان ثابتا بالوحي.
The proof for the establishment of the message (al-risāla) in past times is what has been mentioned: that the substances (al-jawāhir) existing in the world are divided into foods, poisons, and medicines. There is no way to distinguish between some of them and others by experiment (al-tajriba), and bodies cannot endure without consuming foods. Yet we see people who have been guided to them and to knowledge of their natures and to knowledge of the quantities of medicines by which benefit is attained—benefit is not obtained by decreasing them, and harm occurs by increasing them—despite the fact that none of the senses nor intellects can comprehend any of that. For the most perfect of God’s creation in sense and the most abundant in intellect cannot attain that without going to a skilled teacher (ustādh ḥādhiq) from whom he acquires knowledge of that. So it is established that whoever knows that knows it by someone else informing him, not by his sense and intellect, because the knowledge of others falls short of his while they are equal in intellect and sense, until that knowledge reaches the report of one who has knowledge of the true reality of each of those things, because He created them as He created them. In that is the clearest proof for the establishment of the message in the past for someone whom God chose for that and honored by informing him of the natures of these substances. For this reason the people knowledgeable about the natures of these substances who deny the message are forced to admit that knowledge of their natures is revealed (tawqīfī). For whenever it is said to them, 'From whom did you take knowledge of the natures of these things?' they say, 'From Hippocrates.' And if it is said to them, 'From whom did Hippocrates take it?' they say, 'From Asclepius, the Imam whose spirit ascended to heaven and was informed of them.' Likewise, knowledge of the stars, the configuration of the spheres, the natures of the planets, the manner of their movement, their auspicious and inauspicious qualities, and the judgments of their conjunctions—one cannot attain that except through revelation (al-tawqīf), because the senses and intellects are incapable of that. For this reason none of the possessors of sound senses and abundant intellects have grasped that. For this reason the astrologers, when asked about that, were forced to say: 'The beginning of its knowledge came from the one called Hermes the Wise, whose spirit ascended to heaven, and it was in the dominion of the heavens and he knew all that by direct observation.' And some of those who claim knowledge of realities claimed that Hermes is the name of Idris (peace be upon him), according to the people of the Maghrib in a science they know by this name. And the historians claim that the science of the stars was revealed to Idris (peace be upon him). This is among the clearest evidences that all that was established through revelation (al-waḥy) from God Almighty. Likewise, knowledge of the crafts by which livelihood is sustained and the making of covering, shelter, and protection from heat and cold. Likewise, knowledge of the manner of training intractable beasts—things that cannot be known by reflection: for what purpose they were created and by what means they can be trained, their difficulties subdued, and their wild and untamed ones tamed. Likewise, knowledge of the types of trades without which people’s religion and worldly life cannot be established. Likewise, knowledge of what distinguishes their needs in different countries—all that can only be established through revelation (al-tawqīf) because of the incapacity of intellects and senses to grasp it. Likewise, knowledge of the routes of countries. Likewise, knowledge of languages, for there is no way to convention (al-iṣṭilāḥ) except after the establishment of knowledge of one language, so that by knowing that language one can proceed to convention in another language, because there is no way to that except after the conventionalists understand what is in each other’s minds. Therefore, there must be a language established by revelation (al-waḥy).
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage presents a cumulative argument for the necessity of prophethood (al-risāla) in past eras. The author begins with a general proof: the substances (jawāhir) in the world are of three types—foods, poisons, and medicines. Their benefits and harms cannot be reliably distinguished by mere experimentation or by senses and intellect alone. No human, however perfect in sense or intellect, can acquire this knowledge without learning from a skilled teacher. This chain of teaching must ultimately end with a being who knows the true nature of these substances because He created them. That being is God, and He imparts that knowledge to a chosen prophet. The author then reinforces this with historical examples from medicine and astronomy. He points out that even those who deny revelation, when pressed, admit that their knowledge comes from ancient figures who claimed divine inspiration: Hippocrates learned from Asclepius, whose spirit ascended to heaven; astrologers trace their knowledge to Hermes, identified by some with the prophet Idris (Enoch). This shows that the origin of such sciences is divine revelation. The author extends the argument to other domains: crafts for livelihood and shelter, training of animals, types of trade, knowledge of different countries' needs, geography (routes), and languages. In each case, human reason and senses alone are insufficient. For example, language: people cannot agree on a conventional language without first having a common language, which must therefore be originally revealed by God. Thus, all these fields of knowledge point to the necessity of a prophet who received that knowledge from God, confirming that prophethood has been established throughout history.

Key Terms

الجواهر
التجربة
التوقيف
الوحي

إدريس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that empirical knowledge can arise solely from human reason and sense experience.
Correction: The text argues that many critical sciences (medicine, astronomy, etc.) require divine revelation because they are not discoverable by unaided human faculties.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is knowledge of the natures of substances like foods, poisons, and medicines considered a proof of prophethood?
A) Because it can be learned by anyone through experimentation.
B) Because human senses and intellect cannot attain it without a teacher, and the chain ends with a divine source.
C) Because ancient doctors like Hippocrates were prophets.
D) Because substances are created by humans.

Key Takeaway
The necessity of a divine teacher for specialised knowledge proves that prophethood must have been established in the past through revelation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of one skill or piece of knowledge you possess that you did not figure out on your own—you learned it from someone. Who taught you? And who taught them? Trace it back as far as you can. Does it not ultimately lead back to God? Now, how does that chain of teaching make you responsible to use that knowledge for His sake?
?
The passage argues that even language itself must have been revealed by God. Every time you speak, you are using a gift whose ultimate origin is divine. When was the last time you thanked God for the ability to communicate? What would change in your life if you consciously remembered that your words are a trust from Him?
?
The proof shows that human reason alone is not enough to attain certain crucial knowledge. How does that humble your intellectual pride? In what area of your life are you still relying on your own understanding instead of seeking guidance from God's revelation? What step will you take today to surrender that area to Him?

The Necessity of Revelation for Human Knowledge
Al-Nasafi argues that knowledge of various sciences requires divine revelation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Al-Nasafi argues that diverse sciences—from language to warfare—cannot be attained by reason alone and require divine revelation.

Core Idea
Reason cannot reach the sciences of life; revelation is necessary.

Al-Nasafi presents a sweeping argument: many bodies of knowledge that humans rely on daily, such as language, trade routes, and animal training, are beyond the capacity of unaided reason and sensory experience. He points to the tradition of Hermes/Idris and lists numerous examples to show that such knowledge must come from divine revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the list of sciences Al-Nasafi enumerates.
Pay attention to the phrase 'هذا من أبين الدلائل' which marks his key evidence.
2
Identify the central claim
Al-Nasafi claims that knowledge of these sciences is only possible through divine instruction (توقيف). Find where he states this directly.
3
Examine the examples
Review each science mentioned: letters, clothing, animal training, trade, languages, etc. Ask yourself: Could humans have discovered these without revelation?
Think especially about language: how could the first convention occur without a prior language?
4
Understand the reasoning
The argument is: these sciences cannot be attained by senses or intellect (الحواس أو العقل), so they must be from the All-Knowing.
Connect this to the broader Islamic doctrine of prophethood.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider the implications: human knowledge is not self-sufficient; we depend on revelation for foundational sciences.
This counters the idea that human reason alone can achieve all knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حين سئلوا عن ذلك إلى أن قالوا: بدء معرفته من قيل هرمس الحكيم وقد عرج بروحه إلى السماء، فكانت في ملكوت السماوات وعرف ذلك كله مشاهدة. وزعم بعض من ادعى العلم بالحقائق أن هرمس هو اسم إدريس عليه السلام، عند أهل المغرب في علم يعرفونه بهذا الاسم، وأهل التواريخ يزعمون أن علم النجوم نزل على إدريس عليه السلام. وهذا من أبين الدلائل أن ذلك كله ثبت بطريق الوحي من الله تعالى. وكذا العلم بالحرف التي بها قوام المعاش واتخاذ الستر والكن والوقاية من الحر والبرد. وكذا العلم بكيفية رياضة الدواب الصعبة مما ليس يعلم بالتأمل أنها لأي منفعة خلقت وبأي وجه يمكن رياضتها وتذليل صعابها وإيناس نافرها ومستوحشها. وكذا العلم بأنواع التجارات التي لا يقوم للناس دين ولا دنيا إلا بها. وكذا العلم بما يفرق بين حوائجهم فى البلدان لن يثبت إلا بالتوقيف لقصور العقول والحواس عن الوقوف على ذلك. وكذا العلم بطرق البلدان، وكذا العلم بالألسن إذ لا وجه إلى الاصطلاح إلا بعد ثبوت العلم بلسان ليتوصل بمعرفة ذلك اللسان إلى الاصطلاح على لسان آخر إذ لا وصول إلى ذلك إلا بعد وقوف المصطلحين بعضهم على ما في ضمير البعض، فإذا لابد من كون لسان ثابتا بالوحي. وكذا العلم بوجوه أسباب التناسل، والعلم بكيفية تربية الصغار والعلم بتدابير أغذية ما ليس له نطق. وكذا العلم بالسحر وتغيير جواهر الأشياء بأنواع المعالجات. وعلوم محاربة الأعداء. فكان ثبوت العلم بهذه الأشياء مع استنساخ [؟] حصول ذلك بشيء من الحواس أو العقل، دليلاً أن العلم بها كلها توقيف من عند العليم الخبير الذي لا يعزب عنه شيء ولا يخفى عليه خافية، وذلك يكون بالوحي إلى من اصطفاه لرسالته والله الموفق.
When they were asked about that, they said: the beginning of knowledge of it is from Hermes the wise, and his spirit ascended to heaven, and it was in the kingdom of the heavens, and he knew all that by witnessing. And some of those who claimed knowledge of realities claimed that Hermes is the name of Idris (peace be upon him) among the people of the Maghrib in a science they know by this name, and the historians claim that the science of the stars was revealed to Idris (peace be upon him). And this is among the clearest evidences that all that was established by way of revelation from Allah Almighty. Likewise, the knowledge of letters by which livelihood is sustained, and the making of clothing and shelter and protection from heat and cold. And likewise, the knowledge of how to train difficult beasts, which is not known by reflection for what benefit they were created and in what way they can be trained, subdued, and their wild and shy ones tamed. And likewise, the knowledge of types of trades by which people have no religion or worldly life except through them. And likewise, the knowledge of what distinguishes their needs in the lands is only established by divine instruction due to the incapacity of intellects and senses to grasp that. And likewise, the knowledge of routes of lands, and likewise, knowledge of languages, since there is no way to convention except after the establishment of knowledge of a language by which the knowledge of that language enables reaching a convention on another language, since there is no access to that except after the conveners know what is in the conscience of others. Therefore, there must be a language established by revelation. And likewise, the knowledge of the aspects of causes of reproduction, and knowledge of how to raise young ones, and knowledge of managing the nutrition of what has no speech. And likewise, knowledge of magic and changing the essences of things by types of treatments. And sciences of fighting enemies. So the establishment of knowledge of these things, with the negation [؟] of attaining that by any of the senses or intellect, is evidence that knowledge of all of them is divine instruction from the All-Knowing, the All-Aware, from whom nothing is absent and no secret is hidden, and that is by revelation to whom He chooses for His message. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is an argument that many forms of knowledge cannot be attained by reason or senses alone and must be divinely revealed. It begins by mentioning a claim about Hermes/Idris and then states that this is clear evidence that such knowledge comes by revelation. Then it lists various types of knowledge: letters, clothing, housing, taming animals, trade, distinguishing needs of different lands, routes, languages, reproduction, child rearing, feeding animals, magic, changing substances, and warfare. The conclusion is that since these cannot be obtained by senses or intellect, they must be tawqif (divine instruction) from Allah, the All-Knowing, who reveals to His chosen messengers.

Prophethood

Miracles as Proof of Prophethood and Tawatur
Al-Nasafi presents miracles as proofs of prophethood and explains transmission via tawatur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how miracles serve as proofs of prophethood and how their transmission through mutawatir reports yields certain knowledge.

Core Idea
Miracles are God's signs that confirm prophets, and tawatur guarantees their authenticity.

Al-Nasafi explains that miracles (mu'jizat) are the primary evidence for prophethood. He lists examples from various prophets and then discusses how later generations know about these miracles. The key is that these reports are transmitted by many independent chains (tawatur), making collusion on a lie impossible, so we gain certain knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how al-Nasafi structures his argument: first stating the claim, then giving examples, then explaining transmission.
The passage ends mid-sentence; focus on the presented logic.
2
Identify the main claim and examples
What is the main claim? (Miracles prove prophethood). List the miracles mentioned and note they 'break natural habits' (nāqiḍah lil-'ādāt).
Examples include the she-camel from rock, fire cooling for Ibrahim, etc.
3
Understand the transmission modes
How do contemporaries know? (Direct observation). How do later generations know? (Mutawatir report). What does mutawatir produce? (Necessary knowledge, 'ilm ḍarūrī).
Tawatur is a chain of so many narrators that lying is impossible.
4
Reflect on the impossibility of collusion
Why can't the narrators collude on a lie? Because they are diverse in inclinations, opinions, and natures, making agreement on a falsehood impossible.
This argument safeguards the reliability of prophetic reports.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المعجزات دليل لثبوت الرسالة] ثم الدليل على ثبوت الرسالة لبعض الرسل على التعيين ظهور المعجزات الناقضات للعادات على أيدي كثير منهم كخروج الناقة من الصخر، وصيرورة النار بردًا وسلامًا على إبراهيم، وقلب العصا حية، وتسخير الريح والجن والشياطين وتسبيح الجبال، وإلانة الحديد، وإحياء الموتى، وحنين الأسطوانة وشكاية الناقة، وكلام الجمل المسموم ، ونبع الماء من بين الأصابع وغير ذلك مما هي أدلة صدق إدعاء هم الرسالة على ما بينا من كيفية وجه الدلالة. ثم ثبوت ذلك لأهل زمانهم بالمشاهدة ولمن بعدهم بالخبر المتواتر الذي يوجب العلم الضروري، كما أثبت ذلك بالبلدان النائية والأمم الخالية، ولا مجال للتهمة فيه لا بالفسق ولا بالانتفاع لامتناع إجماع الناس الذين لا يتصور تواطؤهم على الكذب على خبر واحد هو في نفسه كذب، لاستحالة اجتماع دواعي الكذب أناس مختلفين جبلوا على أهواء مختلفة، وآراء مشتتة، وهمم متفرقة، وطبائع
Miracles are proof for the establishment of prophethood. Then the proof of the establishment of prophethood for some messengers specifically is the appearance of miracles that break natural habits at the hands of many of them, such as the emergence of the she-camel from the rock, the fire becoming cool and safety for Ibrahim, the turning of the staff into a snake, the subjugation of the wind and jinn and devils, the glorification of the mountains, the softening of iron, the reviving of the dead, the groaning of the pillar, the complaint of the camel, the speech of the poisoned camel, the flowing of water from between the fingers, and other things that are proofs of the truthfulness of their claim to prophethood, as we have explained the manner of the indication. Then its establishment for the people of their time by direct observation, and for those after them by successive report (khabar mutawatir) that produces necessary knowledge, just as that is established in distant lands and past nations. And there is no room for accusation in it, neither by sin nor by benefit, because it is impossible for a consensus of people whose collusion on lying cannot be imagined, for one report that is itself a lie, due to the impossibility of the motives for lying coming together in people of diverse inclinations, scattered opinions, divergent aspirations, and varied natures.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage defines miracles as proofs of prophethood. It begins with a heading that miracles are proof of the establishment of prophethood. Then it states the proof: the appearance of miracles that break natural habits at the hands of many prophets, listing examples: the she-camel from rock for Salih, fire becoming cool for Ibrahim, staff turning into snake for Musa, wind and jinn subjugated for Sulayman, mountains glorifying for Dawud, iron softening, reviving dead for Isa, the pillar groaning, the camel complaining, the poisoned camel speaking, water flowing between fingers for Muhammad, etc. These are proofs of their truthful claim to prophethood. Then it explains the transmission: for contemporaries, it is by direct observation; for later generations, by mutawatir report that yields necessary (self-evident) knowledge. Such tawatur is immune from accusation of sin or interest because it is impossible for a large group of diverse people to collude on a lie, given their different inclinations, opinions, and dispositions.

Key Terms
معجزات
رسالة
خبر متواتر
علم ضروري
ناقضة للعادات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are just stories that cannot be verified.
Correction: Al-Nasafi argues that the mutawatir transmission makes them as certain as direct observation.

Checkpoint
According to al-Nasafi, why does the mutawatir report of miracles yield necessary (ضروري) knowledge?
A) Because all people agree on them.
B) Because the sheer number of narrators makes collusion on a lie impossible.
C) Because the prophets themselves wrote them down.
D) Because the miracles are still happening today.

Key Takeaway
Miracles are divine confirmations of prophethood, and their transmission by tawatur assures their truth.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about a miracle like the water flowing from the Prophet's fingers, do you accept it as certain truth or do you feel a hint of doubt? What would change in your faith if you truly internalized that tawatur makes such reports as reliable as if you had seen it yourself?
?
You trust many things based on widespread reports—news events, historical facts, scientific claims. Why, then, do you sometimes treat reports of miracles with more skepticism? Is it because you assume they cannot happen, or because you haven't examined the strength of their transmission? Challenge yourself to investigate the chains of transmission for at least one miracle mentioned in this lesson.
?
If someone told you that the Prophet's miracles are just stories exaggerated over time, how would you respond using al-Nasafi's argument about the impossibility of collusion among diverse narrators? Would your response be merely academic, or would it affect how you live your daily life as a believer?

The Doubt against Miracles
Presents a skeptic's doubt against prophetic miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the skeptic's argument that miracles cannot serve as evidence for prophethood because they either conform to nature or are impossible.

Core Idea
The skeptic claims miracles are either natural or impossible — neither proves prophethood.

Before we can appreciate the refutation, we must first understand the doubt itself. The skeptic argues that if a miracle occurs naturally, it is no miracle, and if it defies nature, it is impossible — thus prophethood cannot be established by such events. This lesson presents that doubt as a stepping stone to the defense of prophetic miracles.

Guided Path
1
Read the doubt passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Identify the two alternatives the skeptic poses: if the event is natural or unnatural.
The skeptic uses a dichotomy: either within custom or beyond it.
2
Analyze the logical structure
Recognize that the doubt is built on two premises: no evidence from natural events, and no possibility of supernatural events. Consider why the skeptic thinks nature cannot change.
This reflects a naturalist assumption.
3
Reflect on the weakness
The author calls this speech feeble. Think about why someone might find this argument weak even before the refutation.
The author uses strong language to indicate the argument's absurdity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما شبهة من زعم أن لا ثبوت للرسالة إلا بالدليل ولا ثبوت للدليل، فإنه لو كان خارجًا على ما عليه العادة ومجرى الطبيعة فلا دليل فيه، وإن خرج عن العادة ومجرى الطبيعة فهو محال إذ لا تغير للطبائع. فكلام واه لو تفوه به مجنون لتعجب منه، وذلك لما مر أن كل ذلك معاينه من لا يجوز خفاء أمره عليهم لكثرتهم، فكان ما أنكروه من الخروج عن الطبيعة بلا حجة شبهة اعتمدوا عليها ثابتا بالحس الذي هو أوضح طريق العلم وأعلى سبل المعرفة فكان إنكارهم مردودا، وجواز انقلاب الطبيعة ثابتا. يحققه أنهم لو اعتمدوا في ذلك على دليل يتراءى أنه معقول ولا يهتدي بالعقل إلى كيفية رده كان ذلك مردودًا لما أن الدليل العقلي يوجب العلم الاستدلالي والخطأ على الاستدلالي جائز ممكن، وما أنكروه ثابت بالحس الموجب للعلم الضروري الذي لا يجوز عليه الخطأ والغلط، ولابد من رد أحدهما ورد ما يجوز عليه الخطأ والغلط أولى من رد ما لا يجوز عليه ذلك. يحققه أن معرفة ثبوت ما أنكروه ثابت بالحس فكان بطلان دليلهم بالحس، وكل دليل عرف بطلانه ضرورة كان باطلاً أو كان شبهة لا دليلاً فكيف وهم لم يبنوا إنكارهم على شبهة.
As for the doubt of one who claims that prophethood is not established except by evidence and evidence is not established: for if it (the miracle) occurs according to custom and the course of nature, then there is no evidence in it; and if it departs from custom and the course of nature, then it is impossible because natures do not change. So it is feeble speech; if a madman uttered it, one would be amazed at him. That is because, as has passed, all that (miracle) is witnessed by people whose affair it is not possible to conceal from them due to their multitude; thus what they denied of departure from nature, without a proof, is a doubt they relied upon, while it (the departure) is established by sense (al-hiss), which is the clearest path of knowledge and the highest means of cognition. So their denial is rejected, and the permissibility of change of nature is established. He confirms it: if they relied in that upon an argument that appears to be rational and the intellect cannot find a way to refute it, that would still be rejected because rational argument yields speculative knowledge (al-ilm al-istidlali), and error in speculative knowledge is possible and permissible, while what they denied is established by sense which yields necessary knowledge (al-ilm al-daruri) in which error and mistake are not possible. It is necessary to reject one of them, and rejecting that in which error and mistake are possible is more appropriate than rejecting that in which that is not possible. He confirms it: the knowledge of the establishment of what they denied is established by sense, so the invalidity of their argument is established by sense; and every argument known to be invalid necessarily is invalid, or it is a doubt not an argument. So how (could it be otherwise) while they did not base their denial on a doubt?
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage presents a doubt (shubha) and its refutation. The doubt states that prophethood cannot be established because neither natural nor miraculous events can serve as evidence: natural events are not evidence, and miracles are impossible since natures do not change. The author refutes this by first calling such speech feeble, then explaining that the miraculous events are witnessed by so many people that their concealment is impossible. The denial of such events is based on a false assumption, while the events themselves are established by sense perception (al-hiss), which is the clearest path to knowledge. The author then argues that even if the deniers had a rational argument against the miracle, that rational argument yields only speculative knowledge (al-ilm al-istidlali) which is subject to error, whereas sense perception yields necessary knowledge (al-ilm al-daruri) which is not subject to error. When there is a conflict, it is more appropriate to reject the fallible (rational argument) than the infallible (sensory knowledge). Moreover, the occurrence of the miracle is known by sense, so their rational argument is disproven by sense. Any argument known to be invalid necessarily is either false or merely a doubt. Therefore the deniers' position is groundless.

Key Terms
شبهة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That miracles are impossible because nature cannot change
Correction: The author will argue that nature can change, as witnessed by many.

Checkpoint

A) It provides evidence
B) It is impossible
C) It is natural
D) It is uncertain

Key Takeaway
The skeptic denies the possibility of miracles by arguing that any event is either natural (not evidence) or supernatural (impossible).

Refutation through Sensory Certainty
Refutes the doubt by prioritizing sensory certainty over rational inference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why sensory perception of miracles is superior to rational arguments against them.

Core Idea
Sensory knowledge is necessary and infallible; rational knowledge is speculative and fallible.

Having presented the doubt, the author now mounts a powerful refutation. He argues that the miracles were witnessed by multitudes, providing sensory certainty. Moreover, even if the skeptics had a rational argument against miracles, sensory knowledge takes precedence because it is necessary and infallible. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic from 'فكلام واه' to the end. Follow the author's argument step by step.
Note the shift from dismissing the doubt to establishing sensory certainty.
2
Distinguish the two types of knowledge
Identify where the author contrasts speculative knowledge (علم استدلالي) and necessary knowledge (علم ضروري). Understand why necessary knowledge is considered superior.
This is a key epistemological principle.
3
Apply the conflict resolution
The author argues that when sensory and rational knowledge conflict, the fallible rational must be rejected. See how he applies this to the miracle example.
The miracles are known by sense, so any rational objection must yield.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما شبهة من زعم أن لا ثبوت للرسالة إلا بالدليل ولا ثبوت للدليل، فإنه لو كان خارجًا على ما عليه العادة ومجرى الطبيعة فلا دليل فيه، وإن خرج عن العادة ومجرى الطبيعة فهو محال إذ لا تغير للطبائع. فكلام واه لو تفوه به مجنون لتعجب منه، وذلك لما مر أن كل ذلك معاينه من لا يجوز خفاء أمره عليهم لكثرتهم، فكان ما أنكروه من الخروج عن الطبيعة بلا حجة شبهة اعتمدوا عليها ثابتا بالحس الذي هو أوضح طريق العلم وأعلى سبل المعرفة فكان إنكارهم مردودا، وجواز انقلاب الطبيعة ثابتا. يحققه أنهم لو اعتمدوا في ذلك على دليل يتراءى أنه معقول ولا يهتدي بالعقل إلى كيفية رده كان ذلك مردودًا لما أن الدليل العقلي يوجب العلم الاستدلالي والخطأ على الاستدلالي جائز ممكن، وما أنكروه ثابت بالحس الموجب للعلم الضروري الذي لا يجوز عليه الخطأ والغلط، ولابد من رد أحدهما ورد ما يجوز عليه الخطأ والغلط أولى من رد ما لا يجوز عليه ذلك. يحققه أن معرفة ثبوت ما أنكروه ثابت بالحس فكان بطلان دليلهم بالحس، وكل دليل عرف بطلانه ضرورة كان باطلاً أو كان شبهة لا دليلاً فكيف وهم لم يبنوا إنكارهم على شبهة.
As for the doubt of one who claims that prophethood is not established except by evidence and evidence is not established: for if it (the miracle) occurs according to custom and the course of nature, then there is no evidence in it; and if it departs from custom and the course of nature, then it is impossible because natures do not change. So it is feeble speech; if a madman uttered it, one would be amazed at him. That is because, as has passed, all that (miracle) is witnessed by people whose affair it is not possible to conceal from them due to their multitude; thus what they denied of departure from nature, without a proof, is a doubt they relied upon, while it (the departure) is established by sense (al-hiss), which is the clearest path of knowledge and the highest means of cognition. So their denial is rejected, and the permissibility of change of nature is established. He confirms it: if they relied in that upon an argument that appears to be rational and the intellect cannot find a way to refute it, that would still be rejected because rational argument yields speculative knowledge (al-ilm al-istidlali), and error in speculative knowledge is possible and permissible, while what they denied is established by sense which yields necessary knowledge (al-ilm al-daruri) in which error and mistake are not possible. It is necessary to reject one of them, and rejecting that in which error and mistake are possible is more appropriate than rejecting that in which that is not possible. He confirms it: the knowledge of the establishment of what they denied is established by sense, so the invalidity of their argument is established by sense; and every argument known to be invalid necessarily is invalid, or it is a doubt not an argument. So how (could it be otherwise) while they did not base their denial on a doubt?

Commentary
This passage presents a doubt (shubha) and its refutation. The doubt states that prophethood cannot be established because neither natural nor miraculous events can serve as evidence: natural events are not evidence, and miracles are impossible since natures do not change. The author refutes this by first calling such speech feeble, then explaining that the miraculous events are witnessed by so many people that their concealment is impossible. When there is a conflict, it is more appropriate to reject the fallible (rational argument) than the infallible (sensory knowledge). Moreover, the occurrence of the miracle is known by sense, so their rational argument is disproven by sense. Any argument known to be invalid necessarily is either false or merely a doubt. Therefore the deniers' position is groundless.
